					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Austroasiatic language of Meghalaya state, India</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with the Indo-Aryan <a href="/wiki/Kh%C4%81%E1%B9%A3i_language" title="Khāṣi language">Khāṣi language</a> of Jammu and Kashmir or <a href="/wiki/Khas_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Khas language">Khas language</a> of Nepal.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox vevent"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above above" style="font-size:125%; color: black; background-color: lightcoral;">Khasi</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-subheader" style="font-size:110%; color: black; background-color: lightcoral;"><i><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">Ka Ktien Khasi</i></span></i>, ক ক্ত্যেন খসি</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Pronunciation</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><span class="IPA nowrap" lang="kha-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ka<span class="wrap"> </span>kt̪eːn<span class="wrap"> </span>kʰasi/</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Native&#160;to</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Region</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Meghalaya" title="Meghalaya">Meghalaya</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Ethnicity</th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Khasi_people" title="Khasi people">Khasi</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Native speakers</div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;">1 million&#160;(2011 census)<sup id="cite_ref-e25_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e25-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;"><span class="wrap"><a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">Language family</a></span></div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><div style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Austroasiatic</a>
<ul style="line-height:100%; margin-left:1.35em;padding-left:0"><li>
<a href="/wiki/Khasi%E2%80%93Palaungic_languages" title="Khasi–Palaungic languages">Khasi-Palaungic</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Khasic_languages" title="Khasic languages">Khasic</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li>Khasi-Pnar-Lyngngam<ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><b>Khasi</b></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;"><span class="wrap"><a href="/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">Writing system</a></span></div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin</a> (Khasi alphabet) <br /><a href="/wiki/Bengali-Assamese_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengali-Assamese script">Bengali-Assamese</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="color: black; background-color: lightcoral;">Language codes</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-2" title="ISO 639-2">ISO 639-2</a></span></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code><span class="plainlinks"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.loc.gov/standards/iso639-2/php/langcodes_name.php?code_ID=231">kha</a></span></code></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-3" title="ISO 639-3">ISO 639-3</a></span></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code><a href="https://iso639-3.sil.org/code/kha" class="extiw" title="iso639-3:kha">kha</a></code></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><i><a href="/wiki/Glottolog" title="Glottolog">Glottolog</a></i></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://glottolog.org/resource/languoid/id/khas1269">khas1269</a></code></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="/wiki/File:Khasi_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Khasi_map.png/320px-Khasi_map.png" decoding="async" width="320" height="318" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Khasi_map.png/480px-Khasi_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Khasi_map.png/640px-Khasi_map.png 2x" data-file-width="767" data-file-height="762" /></a></span><div style="text-align:left;">Khasi-speaking areas</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Khasi</b> (<span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">Ka Ktien Khasi</i></span>) is an <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_languages" title="Austroasiatic languages">Austroasiatic language</a> with just over a million speakers in north-east India, primarily the <a href="/wiki/Khasi_people" title="Khasi people">Khasi people</a> in the state of <a href="/wiki/Meghalaya" title="Meghalaya">Meghalaya</a>. It has associate official status in some districts of this state. The closest relatives of Khasi are the other languages in the <a href="/wiki/Khasic_languages" title="Khasic languages">Khasic group</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Shillong_Plateau" title="Shillong Plateau">Shillong Plateau</a>; these include <a href="/wiki/Pnar_language" title="Pnar language">Pnar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyngngam_language" title="Lyngngam language">Lyngngam</a> and <a href="/wiki/War_language" title="War language">War</a>.
</p><p>Khasi is written using the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a>. In the first half of the 19th century, attempts to write Khasi in <a href="/wiki/Bengali-Assamese_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengali-Assamese script">Bengali-Assamese script</a> met with little success.<sup id="cite_ref-Script_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Script-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" /></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution_and_status">Geographic distribution and status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geographic distribution and status"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Khasi is natively spoken by 1,038,000 people in India (as of 2011). It is the first language of one-third of the population of <a href="/wiki/Meghalaya" title="Meghalaya">Meghalaya</a>, or 997,000,<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and its speakers are mostly found in the <a href="/wiki/Khasi_Hills" title="Khasi Hills">Khasi Hills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jaintia_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Jaintia Hills">Jaintia Hills</a> regions. There are also small Khasi-speaking communities in neighbouring states of India,<sup id="cite_ref-e25_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e25-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> the largest of which is in <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>: 34,600 people.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2011_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2011-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> There is also a very small number of speakers in Bangladesh.<sup id="cite_ref-e25_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e25-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Khasi has been an associate <a href="/wiki/Languages_with_official_status_in_India" title="Languages with official status in India">official language</a> of some districts within Meghalaya since 2005, and as of 2012, was no longer considered <a href="/wiki/Endangered_language" title="Endangered language">endangered</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> There are demands to include this language to the <a href="/wiki/Eighth_Schedule_to_the_Constitution_of_India" title="Eighth Schedule to the Constitution of India">Eighth Schedule to the Constitution of India</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A sizeable number of books have been published in Khasi, including novels, poetry, religious works, school textbooks and non-fiction. The most famous Khasi poet is <a href="/w/index.php?title=U_Soso_Tham&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="U Soso Tham (page does not exist)">U Soso Tham</a> (1873–1940),<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> whose death is commemorated annually as a <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_India" title="Public holidays in India">regional holiday</a> in the state of Meghalaya.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Khasi has a good presence on the internet, including blogs and several online newspapers.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">Dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Dialects"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Khasi has significant dialectal variation, and this presents a challenge with regard to classifying the <a href="/wiki/Khasic_languages" title="Khasic languages">Khasic languages</a>. 
</p><p>Some dialects of Khasi include: 
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cherrapunji" title="Cherrapunji">Sohra</a> Khasi</li>
<li>Mylliem Khasi</li>
<li>Mawlai Khasi</li>
<li>Nongkrem Khasi</li>
<li>War Khasi, not to be confused with the closely associated <a href="/wiki/War_language" title="War language">War language</a><sup id="cite_ref-Bradley_Mohanty_2023_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradley_Mohanty_2023-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Bhoi Khasi</li>
<li>Nonglung</li></ul>
<p>In addition, <a href="/wiki/Pnar_language" title="Pnar language">Pnar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maharam_language" title="Maharam language">Maram</a> (including Langrin)<sup id="cite_ref-Nagaraja_1993_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nagaraja_1993-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Lyngngam_language" title="Lyngngam language">Lyngngam</a> have been listed as types of Khasi, although more recent studies seem to indicate that these are sister languages to Khasi, and that Khasi actually began as a marginal Pnar dialect.<sup id="cite_ref-Sidwell_GoogleSites_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sidwell_GoogleSites-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bhoi, from <a href="/wiki/Nongpoh" title="Nongpoh">Nongpoh</a>, and Nonglung from Umsning, in <a href="/wiki/Ri-Bhoi_district" title="Ri-Bhoi district">Ri Bhoi District</a>, differ substantially from Standard Khasi in their <a href="/wiki/Syntax" title="Syntax">word order</a>. They are distinct enough from Standard Khasi to be sometimes considered separate languages,<sup id="cite_ref-Nagaraja_1993_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nagaraja_1993-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> with Bhoi sometimes classified as intermediate between Khasi and Pnar,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and Nonglung being part of Mnar,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> variously classified as a type of War or of Pnar.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On the other hand, Sohra and War Khasi are lexically very similar.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The Sohra dialect is taken as Standard Khasi, as it was the first dialect to be written in <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet" title="Bengali alphabet">Bengali</a> scripts by the British.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradley_Mohanty_2023_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradley_Mohanty_2023-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nagaraja_1993_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nagaraja_1993-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> While Standard Khasi is spoken by majority in Shillong, it is in turn significantly different from the other Shillong dialects (eight at most) which form a <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">dialect continuum</a> across the capital region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2023)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This section discusses mainly the <a href="/wiki/Phonology" title="Phonology">phonology</a> of Standard Khasi as spoken in and around the capital city, Shillong.
</p><p>Khasi, mainly spoken in Meghalaya, is surrounded by unrelated languages: <a href="/wiki/Assamese_language" title="Assamese language">Assamese</a> to the north and east, <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a> to the south (both <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan languages</a>), <a href="/wiki/Garo_language" title="Garo language">Garo</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Tibeto-Burman language">Tibeto-Burman language</a>) to the west, and a plethora of other Tibeto-Burman languages including <a href="/wiki/Meithei_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Meithei language">Manipuri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mizo_language" title="Mizo language">Mizo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bodo_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Bodo language">Bodo</a>.
</p><p>Although over the course of time, language change has occurred, Khasi retains some distinctive features:
</p>
<ul><li>Khasi remains a stress language, without <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">tones</a>, unlike many of its Tibeto-Burman neighbors.</li>
<li>Like its Mon-Khmer relatives, Khasi has a large inventory of <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phonemic</a> vowels (see below)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Syllable" title="Syllable">syllable structure</a> of Khasi words resembles that of many Mon-Khmer languages, with many lexical items showing a CCVC shape, in which many combinations of consonants are possible in the onset (see examples below).</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consonants">Consonants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Consonants"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Script">Script</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Script"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485"><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2022</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Before British colonization, some of the Khasi Syiems (Royals) used to keep official records and communicate with one another on paper primarily using the Bengali script. <a href="/wiki/William_Carey_(missionary)" title="William Carey (missionary)">William Carey</a> wrote the language with the <a href="/wiki/Bengali_alphabet" title="Bengali alphabet">Bengali script</a> between 1813 and 1838. A large number of Khasi books were written in the Bengali script, including the famous book <i>Ka Niyom Jong Ki Khasi</i> or <i>The Religion of the Khasis</i>, which is an important work on the Khasi religion. 
</p><p>The Welsh <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jones_(missionary)" title="Thomas Jones (missionary)">Thomas Jones</a>, arrived in <a href="/wiki/Cherrapunji" title="Cherrapunji">Sohra</a> on June 22, 1841, and proceeded to write down the local language in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a>. As a result, the modified Latin alphabet of the language has a few similarities with the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh alphabet">Welsh alphabet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The first journal in Khasi was <i>U Nongkit Khubor</i> (The Messenger) published at <a href="/wiki/Mawphlang" title="Mawphlang">Mawphlang</a> in 1889 by <a href="/wiki/William_Williams_(missionary)" title="William Williams (missionary)">William Williams</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Khasi_alphabet">Khasi alphabet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Khasi alphabet"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Khasi in Latin script has a different system, distinct from that of English. Khasi uses a 23-letter alphabet by removing the letters c, f, q, v, x and z from the basic Latin alphabet and adding the diacritic letters ï and ñ, and the digraph ng, which is treated as a letter in its own right. The diagraph ng is also present in Welsh alphabet.
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">

<p><b>Note</b>
</p>
<ul><li>Vowel length is not usually marked in the orthography, although it can be marked optionally by an <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">acute accent</a> (<i>s<b>i</b>m</i> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/sim/</span> "bird" vs. <i>r<b>í</b> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/riː/</span> "country").<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></i></li>
<li>The peculiar placement of <i>k</i> is due to it replacing <i>c</i>. <i>c</i> and <i>ch</i> were originally used in place of <i>k</i> and <i>kh</i>. When <i>c</i> was removed from the alphabet, <i>k</i> was put in its place.</li>
<li>The inclusion of <i>g</i> is only due to its presence in the letter ng. It is not used independently in any word of native origin.</li>
<li><i>h</i> represents both the <a href="/wiki/Fricative" title="Fricative">fricative</a> sound as well as the <a href="/wiki/Glottal_stop" title="Glottal stop">glottal stop</a>(ʔ) word-finally.</li>
<li><i>y</i> is not pronounced as in <i>year</i>, but acts as a <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">schwa</a>(ə), and as a <a href="/wiki/Glottal_stop" title="Glottal stop">glottal stop</a> between vowels. The sound in <i> year</i> is written with <i>ï</i>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lost_Khasi_Script">Lost Khasi Script</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Lost Khasi Script"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A local legend tells of how the Khasi people received their script from God, and that subsequently the Khasi people lost their script in a great flood.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, it was reported that there is evidence of an <a href="/wiki/Undeciphered_writing_systems" title="Undeciphered writing systems">undeciphered script</a>, currently stored at the Kamarupa Anusandhan Samity Library in <a href="/wiki/Guwahati" title="Guwahati">Guwahati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a>, that is considered to be Khasi in origin.<sup id="cite_ref-LostScript_2017_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LostScript_2017-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Grammar"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Khasi is an <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Austroasiatic language">Austroasiatic language</a> and has its distinct features of a large number of consonant conjuncts, with prefixing and infixing.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nouns_and_noun_phrases">Nouns and noun phrases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Nouns and noun phrases"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Word_order">Word order</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Word order"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The order of elements in a Khasi noun phrase is
(Case marker)-(Demonstrative)-(Numeral)-(Classifier)-(Article)-Noun-(Adjective)-(Prepositional phrase)-(Relative clause), as can be seen from the following examples:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ar</p><p style="margin: 0px;">two</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tylli</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="classifier" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ki</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sim</p><p style="margin: 0px;">bird</p></div><p style="display: none;">ar tylli ki sim</p><p style="display: none;">two CL PL bird</p><p style="clear: left;">'two birds'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kato</p><p style="margin: 0px;">that:<abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kynthei</p><p style="margin: 0px;">girl</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kaba</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr>-relative</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">wan</p><p style="margin: 0px;">come</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mynnin</p><p style="margin: 0px;">yesterday</p></div><p style="display: none;">kato ka kynthei kaba wan mynnin</p><p style="display: none;">that:FEM FEM girl FEM-relative come yesterday</p><p style="clear: left;">'that girl who came yesterday'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kmie</p><p style="margin: 0px;">mother</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">jong</p><p style="margin: 0px;">of</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">phi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">you</p></div><p style="display: none;">ka kmie jong phi</p><p style="display: none;">FEM mother of you</p><p style="clear: left;">'your mother'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender">Gender</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Gender"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Khasi has a pervasive gender system.  There are four genders in this language:
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>Gender markers in Khasi
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Marker</th>
<th>Gender
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">u</i></span>
</td>
<td>masculine
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">ka</i></span>
</td>
<td>feminine
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">i</i></span>
</td>
<td>diminutive
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">ki</i></span>
</td>
<td>plural
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Humans and domestic animals have their natural gender:
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">ka kmie</i></span> "mother"</dd>
<dd><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">u kpa</i></span>  "father"</dd>
<dd><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">ka syiar</i></span> "hen"</dd>
<dd><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">u syiar</i></span> "rooster"</dd></dl>
<p>Rabel (1961) writes: "the structure of a noun gives no indication of its gender, nor does its meaning, but Khasi natives are of the impression that nice, small creatures and things are feminine while big, ugly creatures and things are masculine....This impression is not borne out by the facts. There are countless examples of desirable and lovely creatures with masculine gender as well as of unpleasant or ugly creatures with feminine gender"
</p><p>Though there are several counterexamples, Rabel says that there is some semantic regularity in the assignment of gender for the following semantic classes:
</p>
<table>
<tbody><tr>
<td><b>Feminine</b>
</td>
<td><b>Masculine</b>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>times, seasons
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>clothes
</td>
<td>reptiles, insects, flora, trees
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>physical features of nature
</td>
<td>heavenly bodies
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>manufactured articles
</td>
<td>edible raw material
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>tools for polishing
</td>
<td>tools for hammering, digging
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>trees of soft fibre
</td>
<td>trees of hard fibre
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The matrilineal aspect of the society can also be observed in the general gender assignment, where so, all central and primary resources associated with day-to-day activities are signified as Feminine; whereas Masculine signifies the secondary, the dependent or the insignificant.
</p>
<table>
<tbody><tr>
<td><b>Feminine</b>
</td>
<td><b>Masculine</b>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Sun (Ka Sngi)
</td>
<td>Moon (U Bnai)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Wood (Ka Dieng)
</td>
<td>Tree (U Dieng)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Honey (Ka Ngap)
</td>
<td>Bee (U Ngap)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>House (Ka Ïing)
</td>
<td>Column (U Rishot)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Cooked rice (Ka Ja)
</td>
<td>Uncooked rice (U Khaw)
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Note: However do note that there are no such universal rules for gender assignment of nouns in Khasi. There are a lot of exceptions and one such is <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">syntiew (flower)</i></span> which is stereotypically considered feminine but is accompanied with masculine gender signifier "u" i.e. <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">u syntiew</i></span>. This gender assignment to nouns is highly depended on what the native speakers assign the noun which they all naturally agree upon but which can vary sometimes like according to the mood or tone.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Classifiers">Classifiers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Classifiers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Khasi has a classifier system, apparently used only with numerals.  Between the numeral and noun, the classifier <i>tylli</i> is used for non-humans, and the classifier <i>ngut</i> is used for humans, e.g.
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Don</p><p style="margin: 0px;">there:are</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ar</p><p style="margin: 0px;">two</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tylli</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="classifier" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ki</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sim</p><p style="margin: 0px;">bird</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ha</p><p style="margin: 0px;">in</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ruh.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">cage</p></div><p style="display: none;">Don ar tylli ki sim ha ruh.</p><p style="display: none;">there:are two CL PL bird in cage</p><p style="clear: left;">'There are two birds in the cage.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Don</p><p style="margin: 0px;">there:are</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">lai</p><p style="margin: 0px;">three</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ngut</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="classifier" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">CL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ki</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Sordar</p><p style="margin: 0px;">chief</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ha</p><p style="margin: 0px;">in</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">shnong.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">village</p></div><p style="display: none;">Don lai ngut ki Sordar ha shnong.</p><p style="display: none;">there:are three CL PL chief in village</p><p style="clear: left;">'There are three chiefs in the village.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjectives">Adjectives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Adjectives"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is some controversy about whether Khasi has a class of adjectives.  Roberts cites examples like the following:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">u</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">briew</p><p style="margin: 0px;">man</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ba-bha</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="relative(izer)" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">REL</abbr>-good</p></div><p style="display: none;">u briew ba-bha</p><p style="display: none;">MASC man REL-good</p><p style="clear: left;">'a good man'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>In nearly all instances of attributive adjectives, the apparent adjective has the prefix /ba-/, which seems to be a relativiser.  There are, however, a few adjectives without the /ba-/ prefix:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">u</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">'riew</p><p style="margin: 0px;">man</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">sníew</p><p style="margin: 0px;">bad</p></div><p style="display: none;">u 'riew sníew</p><p style="display: none;">MASC man bad</p><p style="clear: left;">'a bad man'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>When the adjective is the main predicate, it may appear without any verb 'be':
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">U</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ksew</p><p style="margin: 0px;">dog</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">u</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">lamwir.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">restless</p></div><p style="display: none;">U ksew u lamwir.</p><p style="display: none;">MASC dog MASC restless</p><p style="clear: left;">'The dog is restless.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>In this environment, the adjective is preceded by an agreement marker, like a verb.  Thus it may be that Khasi does not have a separate part of speech for adjectives, but that they are a subtype of verb.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prepositions_and_prepositional_phrases">Prepositions and prepositional phrases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Prepositions and prepositional phrases"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Khasi appears to have a well-developed group of prepositions, among them
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">bad</i></span> "with, and"</li>
<li><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">da</i></span> "with (instrumental)"</li>
<li><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">na</i></span> "from"</li>
<li><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">ha</i></span> "in, at"</li>
<li><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">sha</i></span> "in, at"</li>
<li><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">jong</i></span> "of"</li></ul>
<p>The following are examples of prepositional phrases:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kmie</p><p style="margin: 0px;">mother</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">jong</p><p style="margin: 0px;">of</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">phi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">you</p></div><p style="display: none;">ka kmie jong phi</p><p style="display: none;">FEM mother of you</p><p style="clear: left;">'your mother'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">u</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">slap</p><p style="margin: 0px;">rain</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">u</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ther</p><p style="margin: 0px;">pour</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">na</p><p style="margin: 0px;">from</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">bneng</p><p style="margin: 0px;">sky</p></div><p style="display: none;">u slap u ther na ka bneng</p><p style="display: none;">MASC rain MASC pour from FEM sky</p><p style="clear: left;">'Rain poured from the sky.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verbs_and_verb_phrases">Verbs and verb phrases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Verbs and verb phrases"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Agreement">Agreement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Agreement"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Verbs agree with 3rd person subjects in gender, but there is no agreement for non-3rd persons (Roberts 1891):
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th></th>
<th>Singular</th>
<th>Plural
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><b>1st person</b></td>
<td>nga thoh 'I write'</td>
<td>ngi thoh 'we write’
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b>2nd person</b></td>
<td>me thoh 'he (masc) writes' pha thoh 'she (fem) writes'</td>
<td>phi thoh 'you (pl). write'
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><b>3rd person</b></td>
<td>u thoh 'he writes' ka thoh 'she writes'</td>
<td>ki thoh 'they write’
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The masculine and feminine markers /u/ and /ka/ are used even when there is a noun phrase subject (Roberts 1891:132):
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">miaw</p><p style="margin: 0px;">cat</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">pah.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">meow</p></div><p style="display: none;">Ka miaw ka pah.</p><p style="display: none;">FEM cat FEM meow</p><p style="clear: left;">'The cat meows.’</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tense_marking">Tense marking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tense marking"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Tense is shown through a set of particles that appear after the agreement markers but before the verb. Past is a particle /la/ and future is /yn/ (contracted to 'n after a vowel):
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Khasi</th>
<th>English
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>U thoh.</td>
<td>He writes.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>U thoh.</td>
<td>He wrote.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>U la thoh.</td>
<td>He has written.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Un thoh</td>
<td>He will write.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Negation">Negation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Negation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Negation is also shown through a particle, /ym/ (contracted to 'm after a vowel), which appears between the agreement and the tense particle.  There is a special past negation particle /shym/ in the past which replaces the ordinary past /la/ (Roberts 1891):
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Khasi</th>
<th>English
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>Um ju thoh.</td>
<td>He doesn't write.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Um shym thoh.</td>
<td>He didn't write.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Um nym thoh</td>
<td>He won't write.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Um dei ban thoh
</td>
<td>He shouldn't write.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Copulas">Copulas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Copulas"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The copula is an ordinary verb in Khasi, as in the following sentence:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">U</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Blei</p><p style="margin: 0px;">God</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">u</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">long</p><p style="margin: 0px;">be</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">jingïeid.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">love</p></div><p style="display: none;">U Blei u long jingïeid.</p><p style="display: none;">MASC God MASC be love</p><p style="clear: left;">'God is love’</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Causative_verbs">Causative verbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Causative verbs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Khasi has a morphological causative /pn-/ (Rabel 1961). (This is spelled <i>pyn</i> in Roberts (1891)):
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Base verb</th>
<th>Gloss</th>
<th>Causative verb</th>
<th>Gloss
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>hiar</td>
<td>come down</td>
<td>pynhiar</td>
<td>let down, export
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>tip</td>
<td>know</td>
<td>pyntip</td>
<td>make known
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>phuh</td>
<td>blossom</td>
<td>pynphuh</td>
<td>beautify
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>ïaid</td>
<td>walk</td>
<td>pyn-ïaid</td>
<td>drive, put agoing
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>jot</td>
<td>torn</td>
<td>pyn-jot</td>
<td>destroy
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>poi</td>
<td>arrive</td>
<td>pyn-poi</td>
<td>deliver
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sentences">Sentences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sentences"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Word_order_2">Word order</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Word order"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Word order in simple sentences is subject–verb–object (SVO):
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">U</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ksew</p><p style="margin: 0px;">dog</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">u</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">bam</p><p style="margin: 0px;">eat</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">doh.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">flesh</p></div><p style="display: none;">U ksew u bam doh.</p><p style="display: none;">MASC dog MASC eat flesh</p><p style="clear: left;">'The dog eats meat.’</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>However, VSO order is also found, especially after certain initial particles, like hangta 'then' (Rabel 1961).
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">hangta</p><p style="margin: 0px;">then</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">la</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PAST</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ong</p><p style="margin: 0px;">say</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">i</p><p style="margin: 0px;">dimin</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">khnai</p><p style="margin: 0px;">mouse</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ïa</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="accusative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ACC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Naam</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Naam</p></div><p style="display: none;">hangta la ong i khnai ïa ka Naam</p><p style="display: none;">then PAST say dimin mouse ACC FEM Naam</p><p style="clear: left;">'Then said the (little) mouse to Naam ... '</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Case_marking">Case marking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Case marking"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Sometimes the object is preceded by a particle ya (spelled ia in Roberts 1891).  Roberts says "ia, 'to', 'for', 'against' implies direct and immediate relation.  Hence its being the sign of the dative and of the <a href="/wiki/Accusative_case" title="Accusative case">accusative case</a> as well"
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">U</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">la</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PAST</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ái</p><p style="margin: 0px;">give</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ïa</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="accusative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ACC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kitab</p><p style="margin: 0px;">book</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ïa</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="accusative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ACC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">nga.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">me</p></div><p style="display: none;">U la ái ïa ka kitab ïa nga.</p><p style="display: none;">MASC PAST give ACC FEM book ACC me</p><p style="clear: left;">'He gave the book to me.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>It appears from Roberts (1891) that Khasi has <a href="/wiki/Differential_object_marking" title="Differential object marking">differential object marking</a>, since only some objects are marked accusative.  Roberts notes that nouns that are definite usually have the accusative and those that are indefinite often do not.
</p><p>Rabel (1961) says "the use of ïa is optional in the case of one object.  In the case of two objects one of them must have ïa preceding.... If one of the objects is expressed by a pronoun, it must be preceded by ïa."
</p><p>Broadly speaking, Khasi marks for eight cases, with the <a href="/wiki/Nominative_case" title="Nominative case">nominative case</a> remaining unmarked, for a total of nine cases.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>Case markers in Khasi
</caption>
<tbody><tr>
<th>Case</th>
<th>Marker
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Nominative_case" title="Nominative case">Nominative</a></td>
<td>(unmarked)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Accusative_case" title="Accusative case">Accusative</a>-<a href="/wiki/Dative_case" title="Dative case">dative</a></td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">ïa</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Ablative_case" title="Ablative case">Ablative</a></td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">na</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Locative_case" title="Locative case">Locative</a></td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">ha</i></span>
</td></tr>

<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">sha</i></span>
</td></tr>

</td></tr>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>All case markers can appear with or without the prenominal markers/articles <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">u</i></span>, <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">ka</i></span>, <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">i</i></span> and <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">ki</i></span>, and are placed before the prenominal markers.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Passive">Passive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Passive"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Khasi has a passive, but it involves removing the agent of the sentence without putting the patient in subject position.  (A type called the 'non-ascensional passive').  Compare the following active-passive pair (Roberts 1891) where the patient continues to have accusative case and remains in the object position:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Ki</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">dang</p><p style="margin: 0px;">contin</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tháw</p><p style="margin: 0px;">build</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ïa</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="accusative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ACC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ïing</p><p style="margin: 0px;">house</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">da</p><p style="margin: 0px;">with</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ki</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="plural number" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PL</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">dieng..</p><p style="margin: 0px;">wood</p></div><p style="display: none;">Ki dang tháw ïa ka ïing da ki dieng..</p><p style="display: none;">PL contin build ACC FEM house with PL wood</p><p style="clear: left;">'They are building the house with wood.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Dang</p><p style="margin: 0px;">contin</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tháw</p><p style="margin: 0px;">build</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ïa</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="accusative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ACC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ïing.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">house</p></div><p style="display: none;">Dang tháw ïa ka ïing.</p><p style="display: none;">contin build ACC FEM house</p><p style="clear: left;">'The house is being built.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>This type of passive is used, even when the passive agent is present in a prepositional phrase:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">La</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PAST</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">lah</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="perfective aspect" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PFV</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">pyniap</p><p style="margin: 0px;">kill</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ïa</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="accusative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ACC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">masi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">cow</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">da</p><p style="margin: 0px;">by</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">U Míet.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">U‍ Miet</p></div><p style="display: none;">La lah pyniap ïa ka masi da {U Míet}.</p><p style="display: none;">PAST PFV kill ACC FEM cow by {U&#8205; Miet}</p><p style="clear: left;">'The cow was killed by U Miet.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Questions">Questions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Questions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Yes–no questions seem to be distinguished from statements only by intonation:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Phi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">you</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kit</p><p style="margin: 0px;">are carrying</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">khoh</p><p style="margin: 0px;">a basket</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Til?</p><p style="margin: 0px;">Til?</p></div><p style="display: none;">Phi kit khoh Til?</p><p style="display: none;">you {are carrying} {a basket} Til?</p><p style="clear: left;">'Will you take a basket, Til? Phin shim ka khoh, Til?</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>Wh-questions don't involve moving the wh-element:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">u</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="masculine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">MASC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">leit</p><p style="margin: 0px;">go</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">shaei?</p><p style="margin: 0px;">where</p></div><p style="display: none;">u leit shaei?</p><p style="display: none;">MASC go where</p><p style="clear: left;">Where is he going?'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Embedded_clauses">Embedded clauses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Embedded clauses"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Subordinate clauses follow the main verb that selects them (Roberts 1891:169):
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Nga</p><p style="margin: 0px;">I</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">tip</p><p style="margin: 0px;">know</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ba</p><p style="margin: 0px;">that</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">phi</p><p style="margin: 0px;">you</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">la</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PAST</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">leh</p><p style="margin: 0px;">do</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ia</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="accusative case" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">ACC</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">kata.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">that</p></div><p style="display: none;">Nga tip ba phi la leh ia kata.</p><p style="display: none;">I know that you PAST do ACC that</p><p style="clear: left;">'I know that you have done that'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<p>Relative clauses follow the nouns that they modify and agree in gender:
</p>
<div class="interlinear" style="margin-left:3em"><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">Ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">samla kynthei</p><p style="margin: 0px;">girl</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka-ba</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr>-relative</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">wan</p><p style="margin: 0px;">come</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">mynhynnin</p><p style="margin: 0px;">yesterday</p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">ka</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="feminine gender" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">FEM</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">la</p><p style="margin: 0px;"><abbr class="gloss-abbr" title="past tense" style="font-variant: small-caps; font-variant-numeric: oldstyle-nums; text-transform: lowercase;">PAST</abbr></p></div><div style="float: left; margin-bottom: 0.3em;margin-right: 1em;"><p lang="kha" style="margin: 0px;font-style: italic;">iáp.</p><p style="margin: 0px;">die</p></div><p style="display: none;">Ka {samla kynthei} ka-ba wan mynhynnin ka la iáp.</p><p style="display: none;">FEM girl FEM-relative come yesterday FEM PAST die</p><p style="clear: left;">'The girl who came yesterday has died.'</p><div style="clear: left; display: block;"></div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contractions_and_other_reduced_forms">Contractions and other reduced forms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Contractions and other reduced forms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Contractions">Contractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Contractions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A variety of Khasi prepositions and other words are contracted or reduced both in spoken and written language. One of the most common form of contractions is when a <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">pronoun</i></span> is grouped with the verbs "<span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">yn</i></span>" or "<span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">ym</i></span>" (for e.g. <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">u yn</i></span> contracts to <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">u'n</i></span>). Or when a preposition is grouped with a vowel-like gender identifier such as "<span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">u</i></span>" and "<span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">i</i></span>" (for e.g. <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">ha u</i></span> contracts to <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">h'u</i></span>).
</p>
