<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reduced_words">Reduced words</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Reduced words"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Reduced form of words are common in the Khasi language. Most of the time, one or a couple of letters are dropped at the beginning of a word (for e.g. briew can become 'riew). There's no clear rule behind this process but usually these words that undergo reduction begins with more than one consonants; the reduced word is accompanied by an apostrophe from the start to mark so. The reduced form of the word is still understood by its context of usage and since its last inner syllabus and letters (i.e. <span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">rhyme</i></span>) are always preserved.
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th>Word</th>
<th>Reduced form
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>briew</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'riew</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>khlaw</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'law</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>sla</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'la</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>blei</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'lei</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>shniuh</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'niuh</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>shnong</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'nong</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>lyer</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'er</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>

<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'ti</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>blang</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'lang</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>khñiang</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'ñiang</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>khmat</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'mat</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>shkor</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'kor</i></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>dohkha</td>
<td><span title="Khasi-language text"><i lang="kha">'kha</i></span>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>These reduced forms of words are mostly seen in compound forms where the reduced word is affixed with other words to give rise to new words with new meanings. In compound form, the apostrophe is not used anymore. For e.g. 'riew as in riewkhlaw, riewspah, riewhyndai etc.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_text_in_Khasi">Sample text in Khasi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sample text in Khasi"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Article_1_of_the_Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights">Article 1 of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Article 1 of the Universal Declaration of Human Rights"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><b>Khasi Alphabet</b>
</p><p>Ïa ki bynriew baroh la kha laitluid bad ki ïaryngkat ha ka burom bad ki hok. Ha ki la bsiap da ka bor pyrkhat bad ka jingïatiplem bad ha ka mynsiem jingsngew shipara, ki dei ban ïatrei bynrap lang.
</p><p><small>(<i>Jinis 1 jong ka Jingpynbna-Ïar Satlak ïa ki Hok Longbriew-Manbriew</i>)</small>
</p><p><b>Assamese script</b>
যা কি বৃনৰ‌্যের বাৰহ লা খা লাচলোছ বাড কী যৰূঙ্কট হা কি বুৰম বাড ক হক. হাকি লা বৃস্যপ দা ক বৰ-পৃৰ্খট বাড ক চিংযাতিপলেম বাড হা ক মৃন্স্যেম চিংস্ঙেউ শীপাৰা, কী দেই বাণ যত্ৰেই বৃনৰাপ লাং.
</p><p><small>(<i>জিনিস বানৃঙ্গং জং ক চিংপৃনবৃনা-যাৰ সত্লাক যা কি হক লংব্ৰ্যের-মানব্র্যের.</i>)</small>
</p><p><b>IPA</b>
</p><p>jaː ki bɨnreʊ baːrɔʔ laː kʰaː lacloc bat ki jaːrɨŋkat haː kaː burɔm bat ki hɔk. haː ki laː bsjap daː kaː bɔːr pɨrkʰat bat kaː dʒɪŋjaːtɪplɛm bat haː kaː mɨnseːm dʒɨŋsŋɛʊ ʃiparaː ki dɛɪ ban jaːtrɛɪ bɨnrap laŋ
</p><p>(<i>dʒinɪs banɨŋkɔŋ dʒɔŋ kaː dʒɨŋpɨnbnaː-jaːr satlak jaː ki hɔk lɔŋbreʊ manbreʊ</i>)
</p><p><b>Gloss</b>
</p><p>To the human all are born free and they equal in the dignity and the rights. In them are endowed with the power thought and the conscience and in the spirit feeling fraternity they should to work assist together.
</p><p>(<i>Article first of the Declaration Universal of the Rights Humanity</i>)
</p><p><b>Translation</b>
</p><p>All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They are endowed with reason and conscience and should work towards each other in a spirit of brotherhood.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Basic_vocabulary">Basic vocabulary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khasi_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Basic vocabulary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</td></tr>

</td></tr>
<tr>

</td>
<td>What is the price of this? (une is masculine gender, kane is feminine gender and ine
<p>is neutral gender)
</p>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Leit suk.
</td>
<td>Happy journey
</td></tr>
<tr>

</td>
<td>Literal meaning is "Stay happy.”
</td></tr></tbody></table>
